If BOTH `append` and a non-default `append_action` are set -> error\n2. If `append` is set -> use it (true = APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD, false = OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD)\n3. The header_mutation filter's `encodeHeaders` method (line 183-198) calls `mutateResponseHeaders` which evaluates the headers from the global and per-route configs.\n\nBut this is a separate filter in the filter chain. It shouldn't cause duplication unless... wait, let me think about this.\n\nThe issue says headers are duplicated on local replies. Let me trace through the local reply path:1. Router calls `sendLocalReply()` with a callback\n2. Filter manager's `sendLocalReply()` is called\n3. Filter manager creates a lambda for the EncodeFunctions that calls:   - `finalizeResponseHeaders()` (which applies route-level response_headers_to_add)   - Then calls the modify_headers callback from the router4. This lambda is passed to `Utility::prepareLocalReply()` which calls it at line 718-720\n5. Then `Utility::encodeLocalReply()` is called which eventually calls `filter_manager_callbacks_.encodeHeaders()`\n6. The filter manager then calls `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` (line 1244-1330)\n7. This iterates through encoder filters in reverse order and calls their `encodeHeaders()` methods\n8. Including the header_mutation filter!\n\nSo the question is: does the header_mutation filter apply the SAME headers again?\n\nLooking at the header_mutation filter's `encodeHeaders` (line 183-198):- It calls `config_->mutations().mutateResponseHeaders()` (line 185)\n- Then iterates through route_configs and calls their `mutateResponseHeaders()` (lines 192-194)This is applying mutations from global, VirtualHost, and per-route configs via the header_mutation filter.But are these the SAME as the route-level `response_headers_to_add` from the route config?\n\nActually, I think I see the issue now. The header_mutation filter applies response headers from its configuration, but the router's `response_headers_to_add` are applied via the `finalizeResponseHeaders()` method in the route config.\n\n\nThe route config's `response_headers_to_add` is a separate field from the header_mutation filter's configuration. If both are configured with identical headers, they'd both apply them during encoding—once through `finalizeResponseHeaders()` and again through the header_mutation filter's `encodeHeaders()` call. This would explain the duplication on local replies.\n\nWhen the router sends a local reply for cluster not found, it passes `modify_headers_` as a callback, but this lambda doesn't invoke `finalizeResponseHeaders()` itself. I need to trace whether finalizeResponseHeaders() gets invoked multiple times across different code paths or if there are duplicate lambda applications happening.\n\nThe access log reveals the header appears twice with identical values rather than being overwritten, which points to addReferenceKey() being called instead of setReferenceKey(). This suggests a proto default value issue where append_action isn't configured properly. Looking at header_parser.cc, there's legacy handling for the deprecated append field—if append is true but append_action is unset, it defaults to APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD.\n\nThe proto defines APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD as the default enum value (0), so when users omit append_action entirely, headers get duplicated on repeated applications. However, the user explicitly set OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD in their configuration, so this default behavior shouldn't apply to their case.\n\nThe real issue likely stems from the local reply processing pipeline. When a local reply is generated, prepareLocalReply invokes the modify_headers callback which applies finalizeResponseHeaders(), then encodeLocalReply subsequently calls filter_manager_callbacks_.encodeHeaders() through FilterManager. This dual invocation could be causing headers to be processed multiple times even with the overwrite action {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01DJHzsb7SbykNgv5mG8UaMv","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01SA1X9hhMjfPYQ43Y6Nm1Pq","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Duplicate Response Headers in Envoy Filter Pipeline\n\n## Summary\n\nResponse headers configured via route-level `response_headers_to_add` are being duplicated in local replies generated by the router filter because `finalizeResponseHeaders()` is invoked twice through different call paths: once during local reply preparation in the filter manager's header mutation lambda, and again through the router's callback mechanism or filter chain processing. The filter manager creates a lambda that applies `finalizeResponseHeaders()`, but the router's callback (particularly for direct responses and error replies) may also trigger header finalization, resulting in duplicate header additions when using the default `APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD` behavior for `HeaderValueOption`.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Files and Functions:**\n- **source/common/http/filter_manager.cc**: `DownstreamFilterManager::sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()` (lines 1109-1141) and `DownstreamFilterManager::prepareLocalReplyViaFilterChain()` (lines 1055-1094)\n- **source/common/router/router.cc**: `Filter::decodeHeaders()` (lines 440-530) and `Filter::onUpstreamAbort()` (lines 1387-1413)\n- **source/common/router/header_parser.cc**: `HeaderParser::evaluateHeaders()` (lines 139-213)\n- **api/envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto**: `HeaderValueOption` message definition (lines 428-481)\n\n**The Mechanism:**\n\nThe filter manager wraps the router's `modify_headers_` callback in an additional lambda during local reply processing:\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/http/filter_manager.cc:1123-1129\n[this, modify_headers](ResponseHeaderMap& headers) -> void {\n  if (streamInfo().route() && streamInfo().route()->routeEntry()) {\n    streamInfo().route()->routeEntry()->finalizeResponseHeaders(headers, streamInfo());  // FINALIZE CALL #1\n  }\n  if (modify_headers) {\n    modify_headers(headers);  // Router's callback - potentially contains another finalization\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThis wrapper lambda is passed as `EncodeFunctions.modify_headers_` to `Utility::prepareLocalReply()` (line 1070-1093), where it's invoked at lines 718-720 of `source/common/http/utility.cc`:\n\n```cpp\n// source/common/http/utility.cc:718-720\nif (encode_functions.modify_headers_) {\n  encode_functions.modify_headers_(*response_headers);\n}\n```\n\nFor direct responses, the router's callback (lines 488-502 of router.cc) explicitly calls:\n\n```cpp\ndirect_response->finalizeResponseHeaders(response_headers, callbacks_->streamInfo());  // FINALIZE CALL #2\n```\n\nThis creates a scenario where:\n1. **First finalization**: The filter manager's lambda calls `route_entry_->finalizeResponseHeaders()`, applying route-level `response_headers_to_add`\n2. **Second finalization**: The router's callback then calls `direct_response->finalizeResponseHeaders()` (for direct responses) or `modify_headers_()` which could trigger additional processing\n3. **Result**: Response headers are added twice through overlapping or sequential evaluation paths\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**Filter Manager's Local Reply Preparation (filter_manager.cc:1070-1093):**\n```cpp\nvoid DownstreamFilterManager::sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain(\n    bool is_grpc_request, Code code, absl::string_view body,\n    const std::function<void(ResponseHeaderMap& headers)>& modify_headers, ...) {\n  Utility::sendLocalReply(\n      state_.destroyed_,\n      Utility::EncodeFunctions{\n          [this, modify_headers](ResponseHeaderMap& headers) -> void {\n            if (streamInfo().route() && streamInfo().route()->routeEntry()) {\n              streamInfo().route()->routeEntry()->finalizeResponseHeaders(headers, streamInfo());  // LINE 1125\n            }\n            if (modify_headers) {\n              modify_headers(headers);  // LINE 1128 - calls router's callback\n            }\n          },\n          // ... encode_headers and encode_data functions\n      },\n      Utility::LocalReplyData{is_grpc_request, code, body, grpc_status, is_head_request});\n}\n```\n\n**Router's Direct Response Handler (router.cc:486-503):**\n```cpp\ncallbacks_->sendLocalReply(\n    direct_response->responseCode(), direct_response->responseBody(),\n    [this, direct_response, &request_headers = headers](Http::ResponseHeaderMap& response_headers) -> void {\n      // ... location header setup ...\n      direct_response->finalizeResponseHeaders(response_headers, callbacks_->streamInfo());  // DUPLICATE FINALIZATION\n    },\n    absl::nullopt, StreamInfo::ResponseCodeDetails::get().DirectResponse);\n```\n\n**Router's Error Reply Handler (router.cc:1403-1412):**\n```cpp\nvoid Filter::onUpstreamAbort(...) {\n  callbacks_->sendLocalReply(\n      code, body,\n      [dropped, this](Http::ResponseHeaderMap& headers) {\n        if (dropped && !config_->suppress_envoy_headers_) {\n          headers.addReference(Http::Headers::get().EnvoyOverloaded, ...);\n        }\n        modify_headers_(headers);  // Router's lambda - may not call finalizeResponseHeaders\n      },\n      absl::nullopt, details);\n}\n```\n\n**Header Mutation Logic (header_parser.cc:182-212):**\n```cpp\nfor (const auto& [key, entry] : headers_to_add_) {\n  // ... value formatting ...\n  switch (entry->append_action_) {\n    case HeaderValueOption::APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD:\n      headers_to_add.emplace_back(key, value);  // Will use addReferenceKey (append)\n      break;\n    case HeaderValueOption::OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD:\n      headers_to_overwrite.emplace_back(key, value);  // Will use setReferenceKey (overwrite)\n      break;\n    // ... other cases ...\n  }\n}\n\n// Apply headers\nfor (const auto& header : headers_to_overwrite) {\n  headers.setReferenceKey(header.first, header.second);  // Replaces existing\n}\nfor (const auto& header : headers_to_add) {\n  headers.addReferenceKey(header.first, header.second);  // Appends or adds\n}\n```\n\n**Proto Default Values (api/envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto:474-476):**\n```protobuf\n// Value defaults to APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD\nHeaderAppendAction append_action = 3 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n```\n\nThe proto default for `append_action` is `APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD` (enum value 0), which causes headers to be appended rather than overwritten when called multiple times.\n\n### The Deprecated `append` Field Issue (header_parser.cc:58-71)\n\n```cpp\nif (header_value_option.has_append()) {\n  if (header_value_option.append_action() != HeaderValueOption::APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD) {\n    creation_status =\n        absl::InvalidArgumentError(\"Both append and append_action are set and it's not allowed\");\n    return;\n  }\n  append_action_ = header_value_option.append().value()\n                       ? HeaderValueOption::APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD\n                       : HeaderValueOption::OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD;\n} else {\n  append_action_ = header_value_option.append_action();\n}\n```\n\nThis logic shows that if the deprecated `append` BoolValue field is used, it can override the `append_action` enum field, but protobuf default values for unset fields may cause unexpected behavior.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **source/common/http/** - Filter manager's local reply handling and response header encoding\n2. **source/common/router/** - Router filter's local reply generation and header finalization\n3. **source/common/router/header_parser.cc** - Header value option parsing and application\n4. **api/envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto** - HeaderValueOption proto definition with default values\n5. **source/extensions/filters/http/header_mutation/** - (Potential secondary processing during filter chain)\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Symptom**: Response headers appear twice in HTTP response (e.g., `x-custom-trace: abc123` appears twice)\n2. **Immediate Cause**: Router generates local reply (upstream timeout, connection failure, etc.)\n3. **Root Mechanism**:\n   - Filter manager's `sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()` creates a lambda that wraps the router's callback\n   - This lambda calls `route_entry_->finalizeResponseHeaders()` which evaluates route-level `response_headers_to_add`\n   - The router's callback may also trigger `finalizeResponseHeaders()` (for direct responses) or rely on default proto values\n4. **Header Processing**:\n   - `HeaderParser::evaluateHeaders()` processes headers based on `append_action_`\n   - For APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD (default), headers are added via `addReferenceKey()` which creates duplicates\n   - For OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD, headers should use `setReferenceKey()` but if called twice, both operations succeed\n5. **Filter Chain Encoding**:\n   - Prepared local reply headers are passed to `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()`\n   - Encoder filters run in reverse order and potentially re-process headers\n   - Filter manager's `encodeHeaders()` does NOT call `finalizeResponseHeaders()` again (lines 1244-1330)\n6. **Access Log Observation**: Header appears twice with identical values, visible in `%RESPONSE_HEADERS%` logging\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe root cause is the double wrapping of `finalizeResponseHeaders()` calls during local reply processing:\n\n**Option 1: Deduplicate in Filter Manager** (Recommended)\n- Modify `DownstreamFilterManager::sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()` to NOT wrap the `modify_headers` callback with an additional `finalizeResponseHeaders()` call\n- Instead, let the router's callback handle header finalization directly\n- Update code at filter_manager.cc:1123-1129 and filter_manager.cc:1072-1078 to conditionally apply `finalizeResponseHeaders()` only if the `modify_headers` callback doesn't already handle it\n\n**Option 2: Track Finalization State**\n- Add a flag to indicate that `finalizeResponseHeaders()` has been called\n- Check this flag before calling it again to prevent duplicate processing\n\n**Option 3: Consolidate Header Mutations**\n- Move all header finalization to occur exactly once in `Utility::prepareLocalReply()` or `Utility::sendLocalReply()`\n- Ensure the router and filter manager don't both invoke finalization\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. **Verify the issue**: Enable debug logging in `HeaderParser::evaluateHeaders()` to see when headers are added\n2. **Trace the call stack**: Add instrumentation at `finalizeResponseHeaders()` calls to count invocations per request\n3. **Check append_action values**: Log the actual `append_action_` value being used for each header\n4. **Monitor for default values**: Search for cases where `append_action` is not explicitly set (relying on proto default)\n5. **Test with explicit OVERWRITE_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD**: Verify that headers are still duplicated even with overwrite action\n\n### Files to Modify\n\n- **source/common/http/filter_manager.cc** - Lines 1072-1078, 1123-1129 (remove or conditionally apply `finalizeResponseHeaders()`)\n- **source/common/router/router.cc** - Lines 486-503 (clarify header finalization responsibility)\n- **source/common/router/header_parser.cc** - Lines 58-71 (handle deprecated `append` field more explicitly)\n- **api/envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto** - Lines 474-476 (consider making default explicit or safer)\n\n## Key Insights\n\n1. **Proto Default Values Matter**: The default `APPEND_IF_EXISTS_OR_ADD` for `append_action` means headers append on default, but the code expects explicit values\n2. **Callback Wrapping**: The filter manager wraps the router's callback in another lambda, creating potential for double-processing\n3. **Local Reply Path**: Local replies take a different code path than upstream responses, specifically through `sendLocalReplyViaFilterChain()` which adds the extra wrapping\n4. **Filter Chain Iteration**: Encoder filters run in reverse order, but `encodeHeaders()` itself doesn't re-apply route-level headers (good)\n5. **Deprecated Fields**: The deprecated `append` BoolValue field complicates proto parsing logic and can cause unexpected behavior\n\n## Related Code Locations\n\n- **Filter chain source/common/router/upstream_request.cc:63-75\n- **Response header configuration**: api/envoy/config/route/v3/route_components.proto:495-498\n- **Router context**:
